	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Sacha Baron Cohen</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For the figure skater, see <a href="/wiki/Sasha_Cohen" title="Sasha Cohen">Sasha Cohen</a>.</div>
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">British stand-up comedian, writer, actor, and voice actor</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This <a href="/wiki/Double-barrelled_name#British_tradition" title="Double-barrelled name">British surname is barrelled</a>, being made up of multiple names. It should be written as <i><a href="/wiki/Baron_Cohen" class="mw-redirect" title="Baron Cohen">Baron Cohen</a></i>, not <i><a href="/wiki/Cohen_(surname)" title="Cohen (surname)">Cohen</a></i>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>

<p><b>Sacha Noam Baron Cohen</b> (born 13 October 1971) is an English actor, comedian, screenwriter, director, and film producer.<sup id="cite_ref-birthname_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-birthname-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> He is known for creating and portraying many fictional satirical characters, including <a href="/wiki/Ali_G" title="Ali G">Ali G</a>, <a href="/wiki/Borat_Sagdiyev" title="Borat Sagdiyev">Borat Sagdiyev</a>, <a href="/wiki/Br%C3%BCno_Gehard" title="Brüno Gehard">Brüno Gehard</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Dictator_(2012_film)" title="The Dictator (2012 film)">Admiral General Aladeen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Who_Is_America%3F" title="Who Is America?">Erran Morad</a>, and many others. Like his idol <a href="/wiki/Peter_Sellers" title="Peter Sellers">Peter Sellers</a>, he adopts a variety of accents and guises for his characters and rarely appears out of character.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In most of his routines, Baron Cohen's characters interact with unsuspecting people, documentary style, who do not realise they are being set up for comic situations and self-revealing ridicule. His other work includes voicing <a href="/wiki/List_of_Madagascar_(franchise)_characters#King_Julien_XIII" title="List of Madagascar (franchise) characters">King Julien XIII</a> in the <i><a href="/wiki/Madagascar_(franchise)" title="Madagascar (franchise)">Madagascar</a></i> film series (2005–2012) and appearing in <i><a href="/wiki/Talladega_Nights:_The_Ballad_of_Ricky_Bobby" title="Talladega Nights: The Ballad of Ricky Bobby">Talladega Nights: The Ballad of Ricky Bobby</a></i> (2006), <i><a href="/wiki/Sweeney_Todd:_The_Demon_Barber_of_Fleet_Street_(2007_film)" title="Sweeney Todd: The Demon Barber of Fleet Street (2007 film)">Sweeney Todd: The Demon Barber of Fleet Street</a></i> (2007), <i><a href="/wiki/Hugo_(film)" title="Hugo (film)">Hugo</a></i> (2011), and <i><a href="/wiki/Les_Mis%C3%A9rables_(2012_film)" title="Les Misérables (2012 film)">Les Misérables</a></i> (2012). He made a cameo as a <a href="/wiki/BBC_News" title="BBC News">BBC News</a> Anchor in <i><a href="/wiki/Anchorman_2:_The_Legend_Continues" title="Anchorman 2: The Legend Continues">Anchorman 2: The Legend Continues</a></i> (2013). Three years later, he played an English <a href="/wiki/Football_hooliganism_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Football hooliganism in the United Kingdom">football hooligan</a> brother of an <a href="/wiki/MI6" class="mw-redirect" title="MI6">MI6</a> spy in the comedy film <i><a href="/wiki/Grimsby_(film)" title="Grimsby (film)">Grimsby</a></i> (2016) and co-starred as Time in the fantasy sequel <i><a href="/wiki/Alice_Through_the_Looking_Glass_(2016_film)" title="Alice Through the Looking Glass (2016 film)">Alice Through the Looking Glass</a></i> (2016). Two years after that, created and starred in <i><a href="/wiki/Who_Is_America%3F" title="Who Is America?">Who Is America?</a></i> (2018) for <a href="/wiki/Showtime_(TV_network)" title="Showtime (TV network)">Showtime</a>, his first television project since <i>Da Ali G Show</i>, for which he was nominated for a <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Actor_%E2%80%93_Television_Series_Musical_or_Comedy" title="Golden Globe Award for Best Actor – Television Series Musical or Comedy">Golden Globe Award for Best Actor – Television Series Musical or Comedy</a>.
</p><p>Baron Cohen was named Best Newcomer at the 1999 <a href="/wiki/British_Comedy_Awards" title="British Comedy Awards">British Comedy Awards</a> for <i><a href="/wiki/The_11_O%27Clock_Show" title="The 11 O&#39;Clock Show">The 11&#160;O'Clock Show</a></i>, and since then, he has received two <a href="/wiki/British_Academy_of_Film_and_Television_Arts" title="British Academy of Film and Television Arts">BAFTA</a> Awards for <i><a href="/wiki/Da_Ali_G_Show" title="Da Ali G Show">Da Ali G Show</a></i>, several <a href="/wiki/Emmy" class="mw-redirect" title="Emmy">Emmy</a> nominations, a nomination for an <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Adapted_Screenplay" title="Academy Award for Best Adapted Screenplay">Academy Award for Best Adapted Screenplay</a>, and a <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden Globe">Golden Globe</a> for <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Actor_-_Motion_Picture_Musical_or_Comedy" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden Globe Award for Best Actor - Motion Picture Musical or Comedy">Best Actor</a> for his work in the feature film <i><a href="/wiki/Borat" title="Borat">Borat</a></i>. After the release of <i>Borat</i>, Baron Cohen stated that because the public had become too familiar with the characters, and he would retire Borat and Ali G.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Similarly, after the release of <i><a href="/wiki/Br%C3%BCno" title="Brüno">Brüno</a></i>, Baron Cohen stated he would also retire that title character.<sup id="cite_ref-shed_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shed-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> At the 2012 British Comedy Awards, he received the Outstanding Achievement Award, accepting the award while reprising his Ali G character.<sup id="cite_ref-lifetime_award_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lifetime_award-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, he received the BAFTA Charlie Chaplin <a href="/wiki/Britannia_Awards" title="Britannia Awards">Britannia Award</a> for Excellence in Comedy.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sacha_Baron_Cohen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Baron Cohen was born in west London to <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jewish</a> parents.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> His mother, Daniella Naomi (née Weiser), who worked as a movement instructor, was born in <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bookref1_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bookref1-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> His father, Gerald Baron Cohen (1932–2016), a clothing store owner, was born in London and raised in Wales.<sup id="cite_ref-moment_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-moment-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bwhsosg_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bwhsosg-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Baron Cohen was raised <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jewish</a><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-telegraph_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> and is fluent in <a href="/wiki/Hebrew_language" title="Hebrew language">Hebrew</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Baron Cohen's maternal family were <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Germany" title="History of the Jews in Germany">German Jews</a> who moved to Israel.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bookref1_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bookref1-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> His paternal family were <a href="/wiki/Ashkenazi_Jews" title="Ashkenazi Jews">Ashkenazi Jews</a>, who moved to <a href="/wiki/Pontypridd" title="Pontypridd">Pontypridd</a> and London in the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> His paternal grandfather, Morris Cohen, added "Baron" to his surname.<sup id="cite_ref-bwhsosg_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bwhsosg-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wales1_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wales1-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> His maternal grandmother, who lived in <a href="/wiki/Haifa" title="Haifa">Haifa, Israel</a>, trained as a ballet dancer in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-moment_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-moment-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-borateasy_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-borateasy-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rollingstone_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rollingstone-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-guardian1_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian1-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Baron Cohen has two older brothers: <a href="/wiki/Erran_Baron_Cohen" title="Erran Baron Cohen">Erran</a> and Amnon.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian2002_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian2002-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Erran is a composer and has worked on several of Sacha's films. Baron Cohen's cousin, <a href="/wiki/Simon_Baron-Cohen" title="Simon Baron-Cohen">Simon Baron-Cohen</a>, is an autism researcher.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sacha_Baron_Cohen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Baron Cohen was educated at <a href="/wiki/The_Haberdashers%27_Aske%27s_Boys%27_School" class="mw-redirect" title="The Haberdashers&#39; Aske&#39;s Boys&#39; School">The Haberdashers' Aske's Boys' School</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Independent_school" title="Independent school">independent school</a> in <a href="/wiki/Elstree" title="Elstree">Elstree</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hertfordshire" title="Hertfordshire">Hertfordshire</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> attended the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cambridge" title="University of Cambridge">University of Cambridge</a>, read History at <a href="/wiki/Christ%27s_College,_Cambridge" title="Christ&#39;s College, Cambridge">Christ's College, Cambridge</a>, and graduated in 1993 with upper-second-class honours.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> While a member of the <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_University_Amateur_Dramatic_Club" title="Cambridge University Amateur Dramatic Club">Cambridge University Amateur Dramatic Club</a>, Baron Cohen performed in plays such as <i><a href="/wiki/Fiddler_on_the_Roof" title="Fiddler on the Roof">Fiddler on the Roof</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Cyrano_de_Bergerac_(play)" title="Cyrano de Bergerac (play)">Cyrano de Bergerac</a></i>, as well as in <a href="/wiki/Habonim_Dror" title="Habonim Dror">Habonim Dror</a> Jewish theatre.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian.co.uk_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian.co.uk-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_roles">Early roles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sacha_Baron_Cohen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early roles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:28%;&#32;;"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r887775652">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%;max-width:100%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{margin:0.5em auto 0.8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft p,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright p{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{background-color:#F9F9F9;text-align:center;font-size:larger;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" “ ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" ” ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:360px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{min-width:100%;margin:0 0 0.8em!important;float:none!important}}</style>
<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">"He [Peter Sellers] was this incredibly realistic actor, who was also hilarious and who managed to bridge the gap between comedy and satire."</div>
<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">—Baron Cohen on his greatest influence, fellow British comedian <a href="/wiki/Peter_Sellers" title="Peter Sellers">Peter Sellers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup></cite>
</p>
</div>
<p>After leaving university, Baron Cohen worked for a time as a <a href="/wiki/Fashion_model" class="mw-redirect" title="Fashion model">fashion model</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian.co.uk_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian.co.uk-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> By the early 1990s, he was hosting a weekly programme on Windsor cable television's local broadcasts with <a href="/wiki/Carol_Kirkwood" title="Carol Kirkwood">Carol Kirkwood</a>, who later became a <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> weather forecaster. In 1995, <a href="/wiki/Channel_4" title="Channel 4">Channel 4</a> was planning a replacement for its series <i><a href="/wiki/The_Word_(TV_series)" title="The Word (TV series)">The Word</a></i>, and disseminated an open call for new television presenters. Baron Cohen sent in a tape of himself in the character of Kristo, an <a href="/wiki/Albanians" title="Albanians">Albanian</a> fictional television reporter (who developed into the <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakh</a> <a href="/wiki/Borat_Sagdiyev" title="Borat Sagdiyev">Borat Sagdiyev</a>), which caught the attention of a producer. Baron Cohen hosted <i>Pump TV</i> from 1995 to 1996. <a href="/wiki/Peter_Sellers" title="Peter Sellers">Peter Sellers</a>, known for portraying a wide range of comic characters using different accents and guises, was referred to by Baron Cohen as "the most seminal force in shaping [his] early ideas on comedy".<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1996, Baron Cohen began presenting the youth chat programme <i><a href="/wiki/F2F_(TV_series)" title="F2F (TV series)">F2F</a></i> for <a href="/wiki/Granada_Talk_TV" title="Granada Talk TV">Granada Talk TV</a> and had a small role in an advert for McCain Microchips, as a chef in a commercial entitled "Ping Pong".<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> He took clown training in Paris, at the <a href="/wiki/Philippe_Gaulier#.C3.89cole_Philippe_Gaulier" title="Philippe Gaulier">Ecole Philippe Gaulier</a>, studying under master-clown <a href="/wiki/Philippe_Gaulier" title="Philippe Gaulier">Philippe Gaulier</a>. Of his former pupil, Gaulier says: "He was a good clown, full of spirit".<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Baron Cohen made his first feature film appearance in the British comedy <i><a href="/wiki/The_Jolly_Boys%27_Last_Stand" title="The Jolly Boys&#39; Last Stand">The Jolly Boys' Last Stand</a></i> (2000). Also in 2000, he played the part of <a href="/wiki/Super_Greg" title="Super Greg">Super Greg</a> for a series of TV advertisements for <a href="/wiki/Lee_Jeans" class="mw-redirect" title="Lee Jeans">Lee Jeans</a>; the advertisements never aired, but the website for Super Greg created an internet sensation.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Characters">Characters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sacha_Baron_Cohen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Characters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ali_G">Ali G</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sacha_Baron_Cohen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Ali G">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ali_G" title="Ali G">Ali G</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:AliG-Harv.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/AliG-Harv.jpg/170px-AliG-Harv.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="319" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/AliG-Harv.jpg/255px-AliG-Harv.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/AliG-Harv.jpg/340px-AliG-Harv.jpg 2x" data-file-width="535" data-file-height="1005" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:AliG-Harv.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Baron Cohen as <a href="/wiki/Ali_G" title="Ali G">Ali G</a>, offering a speech at <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard University</a>'s Class Day during <a href="/wiki/Commencement_speech" title="Commencement speech">Commencement ceremonies</a> in 2004</div></div></div>
<p>Baron Cohen appeared during two-minute sketches as his fashion reporter <a href="/wiki/Br%C3%BCno_(character)" class="mw-redirect" title="Brüno (character)">Brüno</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Paramount_Comedy_1" class="mw-redirect" title="Paramount Comedy 1">Paramount Comedy Channel</a> during 1998. He shot to fame when his comic character Ali G, an uneducated, boorish <a href="/wiki/Junglist" title="Junglist">junglist</a>, hailing from <a href="/wiki/Staines" class="mw-redirect" title="Staines">Staines</a> (a suburban town in Surrey, to the west of London), started appearing on the British television show <i><a href="/wiki/The_11_O%27Clock_Show" title="The 11 O&#39;Clock Show">The 11&#160;O'Clock Show</a></i> on <a href="/wiki/Channel_4" title="Channel 4">Channel 4</a>, which first aired on 8 September 1998. A year after the première of the show, <i><a href="/wiki/GQ" title="GQ">GQ</a></i> named him comedian of the year.<sup id="cite_ref-Saunders_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Saunders-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> He won Best Newcomer at the 1999 <a href="/wiki/British_Comedy_Awards" title="British Comedy Awards">British Comedy Awards</a>, and at the <a href="/wiki/British_Academy_Television_Awards" title="British Academy Television Awards">British Academy Television Awards</a> he was nominated for Best British Entertainment Performance.<sup id="cite_ref-Saunders_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Saunders-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Da_Ali_G_Show" title="Da Ali G Show">Da Ali G Show</a></i> began in 2000, and won the <a href="/wiki/British_Academy_Television_Awards" title="British Academy Television Awards">BAFTA</a> for Best Comedy  in the following year.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Also in 2000, Baron Cohen as Ali G appeared as the limousine driver in <a href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)" title="Madonna (entertainer)">Madonna</a>'s 2000 video "<a href="/wiki/Music_(Madonna_song)#Music_video" title="Music (Madonna song)">Music</a>", directed by <a href="/wiki/Jonas_%C3%85kerlund" title="Jonas Åkerlund">Jonas Åkerlund</a>, who was also responsible for directing the titles for <i>Da Ali G Show</i>. Baron Cohen is a supporter of the UK charity telethon <a href="/wiki/Comic_Relief" title="Comic Relief">Comic Relief</a>, which is broadcast on the BBC, and as Ali G interviewed <a href="/wiki/David_Beckham" title="David Beckham">David Beckham</a> and wife <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Beckham" title="Victoria Beckham">Victoria</a> in 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In a 2001 Channel 4 poll Ali G was ranked eighth on their list of the <a href="/wiki/100_Greatest_(TV_series)" title="100 Greatest (TV series)">100 Greatest TV Characters</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> In 2002, Ali G was the central character in the feature film <i><a href="/wiki/Ali_G_Indahouse" title="Ali G Indahouse">Ali G Indahouse</a></i>, in which he is elected to the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">British Parliament</a> and foils a plot to bulldoze a community centre in his home town, Staines.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> His television show was exported to the United States in 2003, with new episodes set there, for <a href="/wiki/HBO" title="HBO">HBO</a>.
</p><p>At the 2012 British Comedy Awards, 13 years after winning Best Newcomer at the 1999 Comedy Awards, Baron Cohen accepted the Outstanding Achievement Award from Sir <a href="/wiki/Ben_Kingsley" title="Ben Kingsley">Ben Kingsley</a> in the guise of Ali G, and stated: "I is grown up now. I ain't living in my nan's house anymore. I is living in her garage".<sup id="cite_ref-lifetime_award_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lifetime_award-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Ali G's interviews with celebrities (often politicians) gained notoriety partly because the subjects were not privy to the joke that Ali G, rather than being a real interviewer, was a comic character played by Baron Cohen. According to <a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a> magazine, Baron Cohen would always enter the interview area in character as Ali G, carrying equipment and appearing to be an inconspicuous crew member. He would arrive with a suited man, whom the interviewee naturally thought was the interviewer. Baron Cohen, as Ali G, would sit down to begin conducting the interview by asking the interviewee some preliminary questions. The interviewee, however, would remain under the impression that the smartly-dressed director would be conducting the interview until short notice prior to cameras rolling: this would grant an advantage of surprise, whereby the interviewee would be less likely to opt out of the Ali interview prior to its start.<sup id="cite_ref-manbehindmustache_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-manbehindmustache-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Borat_Sagdiyev">Borat Sagdiyev</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sacha_Baron_Cohen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Borat Sagdiyev">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Borat_Sagdiyev" title="Borat Sagdiyev">Borat Sagdiyev</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Borat.portrait.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Borat.portrait.png/170px-Borat.portrait.png" decoding="async" width="170" height="201" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Borat.portrait.png/255px-Borat.portrait.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Borat.portrait.png/340px-Borat.portrait.png 2x" data-file-width="423" data-file-height="501" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Borat.portrait.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Baron Cohen as Borat, 2006</div></div></div>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Borat:_Cultural_Learnings_of_America_for_Make_Benefit_Glorious_Nation_of_Kazakhstan" class="mw-redirect" title="Borat: Cultural Learnings of America for Make Benefit Glorious Nation of Kazakhstan">Borat: Cultural Learnings of America for Make Benefit Glorious Nation of Kazakhstan</a></i>, a feature film with his character <a href="/wiki/Borat_Sagdiyev" title="Borat Sagdiyev">Borat Sagdiyev</a> at the centre, was screened at the <a href="/wiki/2006_Toronto_International_Film_Festival" title="2006 Toronto International Film Festival">2006 Toronto International Film Festival</a> and released in the United Kingdom on 2 November 2006, in the United States on 3 November 2006 and Australia 23 November 2006. The film follows Sagdiyev as he and his colleague <a href="/wiki/Azamat_Bagatov" title="Azamat Bagatov">Azamat Bagatov</a> travel the United States to produce a documentary about life in the country, all the while Sagdiyev attempts to enter into marriage with celebrity <a href="/wiki/Pamela_Anderson" title="Pamela Anderson">Pamela Anderson</a>. The film is a <a href="/wiki/Mockumentary" title="Mockumentary">mockumentary</a> which includes interviews with various Americans that poke fun at <a href="/wiki/American_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="American culture">American culture</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Sexism" title="Sexism">sexism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Racism_in_the_United_States" title="Racism in the United States">racism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Homophobia" title="Homophobia">homophobia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antisemitism" title="Antisemitism">anti-Semitism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jingoism" title="Jingoism">jingoism</a>. It debuted at the No. 1 spot in the US, taking in an estimated $26.4&#160;million in just 837 theatres averaging $31,600 per theatre.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Baron Cohen won the 2007 <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden Globe">Golden Globe</a> in the "<a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Actor_-_Motion_Picture_Musical_or_Comedy" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden Globe Award for Best Actor - Motion Picture Musical or Comedy">Best Actor – Musical or Comedy</a>" category, his sixth such award. Although Borat was up for "Best Motion Picture&#160;– Musical or Comedy", the film lost to <i><a href="/wiki/Dreamgirls_(film)" title="Dreamgirls (film)">Dreamgirls</a></i>. On 23 January 2007, he was nominated for an <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Adapted_Screenplay" title="Academy Award for Best Adapted Screenplay">Academy Award for Best Adapted Screenplay</a>. He shared his nomination with the film's co-writers, Ant Hines, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Baynham" title="Peter Baynham">Peter Baynham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dan_Mazer" title="Dan Mazer">Dan Mazer</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Todd_Phillips" title="Todd Phillips">Todd Phillips</a>.
</p><p>Aside from the comic elements of his characters, Baron Cohen's performances are interpreted by some as reflecting uncomfortable truths about his audience. He juxtaposes his own Jewish heritage with the anti-Semitism of his character Borat.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2007, Baron Cohen published a travel guide as Borat, with dual titles: <i>Borat: Touristic Guidings To Minor Nation of U.S. and A.</i> and <i>Borat: Touristic Guidings To Glorious Nation of Kazakhstan</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Book_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Book-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> On 21 December 2007, Baron Cohen announced he was retiring the character of Borat.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Br.C3.BCno_Gehard"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Brüno_Gehard">Brüno Gehard</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sacha_Baron_Cohen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Brüno Gehard">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Br%C3%BCno_Gehard" title="Brüno Gehard">Brüno Gehard</a></div>
<p>Another alter ego Sacha Baron Cohen performed as is '<a href="/wiki/Br%C3%BCno_(character)" class="mw-redirect" title="Brüno (character)">Brüno</a>', a flamboyantly gay Austrian fashion show presenter who often lures his unwitting subjects into making provocative statements and engaging in embarrassing behaviour, as well as leading them to contradict themselves, often in the same interview. Brüno asks the subjects to answer "yes or no" questions with either "Vassup" (what's up) or "Ich don't think so" (No); these are occasionally substituted with "Ach, ja!" (Ah yes!) or "Nicht, nicht" ("Nicht" means "not" in German). In one segment on <i>Da Ali&#160;G Show</i>, he encouraged his guest to answer questions with either "Keep them in the ghetto" or "Train to <a href="/wiki/Auschwitz_concentration_camp" title="Auschwitz concentration camp">Auschwitz</a>".
</p><p>Brüno's main comedic satire pertains to the vacuity and inanity of the fashion and <a href="/wiki/Clubbing_(subculture)" title="Clubbing (subculture)">clubbing</a> world. In May 2009, at the <a href="/wiki/2009_MTV_Movie_Awards" title="2009 MTV Movie Awards">MTV Movie Awards</a>, Baron Cohen appeared as Brüno wearing a white angel costume, a white <a href="/wiki/Jockstrap" title="Jockstrap">jockstrap</a>, white <a href="/wiki/Go-go_boot" title="Go-go boot">go-go boots</a>, and white wings; and did an aerial stunt where he dropped from a height (using wires) onto <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a>. Baron Cohen landed with his face on Eminem's crotch, with his crotch in Eminem's face, prompting Eminem to exit the venue with fellow rappers <a href="/wiki/D12" title="D12">D12</a>. Eminem later admitted to staging the stunt with Baron Cohen.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> After an intense bidding war that included such Hollywood powerhouses as <a href="/wiki/DreamWorks_Pictures" title="DreamWorks Pictures">DreamWorks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sony_Pictures_Entertainment" class="mw-redirect" title="Sony Pictures Entertainment">Sony</a>, and <a href="/wiki/20th_Century_Fox" title="20th Century Fox">20th Century Fox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Universal_Pictures" title="Universal Pictures">Universal Pictures</a> won and paid a reported $42.5&#160;million for the <a href="/wiki/Film_rights" title="Film rights">film rights</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> A number of <a href="/wiki/Shill" title="Shill">shill</a> companies and websites were created in order to draw potential interviewees into interviews by creating an illusion of legitimacy.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Br%C3%BCno" title="Brüno">The film</a> was released in July 2009.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Admiral_General_Aladeen">Admiral General Aladeen</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sacha_Baron_Cohen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Admiral General Aladeen">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/The_Dictator_(2012_film)" title="The Dictator (2012 film)">The Dictator (2012 film)</a></div>
<p>Baron Cohen's 2012 film, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dictator_(2012_film)" title="The Dictator (2012 film)">The Dictator</a></i>, was described by its press as "the heroic story of a dictator who risked his life to ensure that democracy would never come to the country he so lovingly oppressed".<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Baron Cohen played Admiral General Aladeen, a dictator from a fictional country called the Republic of Wadiya.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-officialsite_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-officialsite-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> <i>Borat</i> and <i>Brüno</i> film director <a href="/wiki/Larry_Charles" title="Larry Charles">Larry Charles</a> directed the film.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The main target of the film's satire was <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libyan</a> dictator <a href="/wiki/Muammar_Gaddafi" title="Muammar Gaddafi">Muammar Gaddafi</a>, who was still alive when the film was written.<sup id="cite_ref-freshair_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freshair-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> The producers of the film were concerned it would anger Gaddafi, possibly even resulting in a terrorist attack, so they released deliberate misinformation saying that the film was loosely based on a romance novel written by former <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraqi</a> dictator <a href="/wiki/Saddam_Hussein" title="Saddam Hussein">Saddam Hussein</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-freshair_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freshair-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 26 February 2012, Baron Cohen was allegedly banned from attending the <a href="/wiki/84th_Academy_Awards" title="84th Academy Awards">84th Academy Awards</a> in his role as Admiral General Aladeen but the rumour was denied by the Academy, saying "we haven't banned him, he is lying" but made it clear that "Cohen is not welcome to use the red carpet as a platform for a promotional stunt".<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Baron Cohen eventually appeared at the awards' red carpet with a pair of <a href="/wiki/Amazonian_Guard" title="Amazonian Guard">uniformed female bodyguards</a>, holding an <a href="/wiki/Urn" title="Urn">urn</a> which he claimed was filled with the ashes of <a href="/wiki/Kim_Jong-il" title="Kim Jong-il">Kim Jong-il</a>. The "ashes", which Baron Cohen admitted to Howard Stern on the Tuesday, 8 May 2012 episode of <i>The Howard Stern Show</i> were flour, were "accidentally" spilled onto <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Seacrest" title="Ryan Seacrest">Ryan Seacrest</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Erran_Morad">Erran Morad</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sacha_Baron_Cohen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Erran Morad">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Who_Is_America%3F" title="Who Is America?">Who Is America?</a></div>
<p>Baron Cohen portrays various characters in <i><a href="/wiki/Who_Is_America%3F" title="Who Is America?">Who Is America?</a></i>, the most prominent and controversial being Erran Morad, an Israeli anti-terrorism expert. The character is referred to as a colonel (and later captain, general, major, sergeant, brigadier, sergeant corporal and lieutenant) in the <a href="/wiki/Israel_Defense_Forces" title="Israel Defense Forces">Israeli military</a> and a former agent of <a href="/wiki/Mossad" title="Mossad">Mossad</a> (or "not in the Mossad," as he often interjects). Before <i>Who Is America?</i> aired on Showtime, some conservative public figures made statements saying that Baron Cohen had deceived them while in character.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Hours before the premiere, Showtime uploaded the "Kinderguardians" segment on their YouTube channel, in which Morad explains to <a href="/wiki/Philip_Van_Cleave" title="Philip Van Cleave">Philip Van Cleave</a>, the president of the Virginia Citizens Defense League, of the proposal of a new program where children ages 3 to 16 are armed with guns. He also interviews other conservatives, such as <a href="/wiki/Dana_Rohrabacher" title="Dana Rohrabacher">Dana Rohrabacher</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joe_Wilson_(American_politician)" title="Joe Wilson (American politician)">Joe Wilson</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Joe_Walsh_(Illinois_politician)" class="mw-redirect" title="Joe Walsh (Illinois politician)">Joe Walsh</a>, who are openly supportive. Only <a href="/wiki/Matt_Gaetz" title="Matt Gaetz">Matt Gaetz</a> expresses skepticism of Morad's proposal, and declines to be in his video.
</p><p>In the second episode, Morad teaches <a href="/wiki/Jason_Spencer" title="Jason Spencer">Jason Spencer</a>, a Republican state representative from Georgia, how to detect and repel terrorists by taking pictures up a woman's burqua with a selfie stick, walking backwards while baring his buttocks, and yelling racial epithets. After the airing of the episode, Spencer initially refused to step down, stating that he was exploited by the producers. He eventually did step down on July 31, 2018, leaving the seat vacant.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> In May 2018, Spencer lost his primary to a political novice, Steven Sainz,<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> but was expected to serve the rest of his term until November.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies_and_criticism">Controversies and criticism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sacha_Baron_Cohen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Controversies and criticism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In an interview with former Tory MP politician <a href="/wiki/Neil_Hamilton_(politician)" title="Neil Hamilton (politician)">Neil Hamilton</a> in 2000, Ali G offered Hamilton what was allegedly <a href="/wiki/Cannabis_(drug)" title="Cannabis (drug)">cannabis</a>, which Hamilton accepted and smoked, creating some minor controversy in the British media.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the 2006 <a href="/wiki/MTV_Movie_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="MTV Movie Awards">MTV Movie Awards</a>, Borat introduced <a href="/wiki/Gnarls_Barkley" title="Gnarls Barkley">Gnarls Barkley</a>'s performance of "<a href="/wiki/Crazy_(Gnarls_Barkley_song)" title="Crazy (Gnarls Barkley song)">Crazy</a>",<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> where he made a comment about <a href="/wiki/Jessica_Simpson" title="Jessica Simpson">Jessica Simpson</a>, saying that he liked her mouth and that he could <a href="/wiki/Camel_toe" title="Camel toe">see it clearly through her denim pants</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the 2006 UK premiere of <i>Borat</i>, he arrived in <a href="/wiki/Leicester_Square" title="Leicester Square">Leicester Square</a> in a cart pulled by a mule and a number of "Kazakh women," announcing: "Good evening, gentleman and prostitutes. After this I stay in a hotel in <a href="/wiki/Kings_Cross,_London" title="Kings Cross, London">Kings Cross</a>. We will all drink, wrestle with no clothes on and shoot dogs from the window."<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Baron Cohen has been criticised for the <a href="/wiki/Racist" class="mw-redirect" title="Racist">racist</a> or <a href="/wiki/Prejudice" title="Prejudice">prejudiced</a> comments his characters have made (see <i><a href="/wiki/Da_Ali_G_Show#Controversy" title="Da Ali G Show">Da Ali G Show</a></i>). HBO spokesman Quentin Schaffer has replied to criticism concerning Baron Cohen's characters, "Through his alter-egos, he delivers an obvious satire that exposes people's ignorance and prejudice in much the same way <i><a href="/wiki/All_in_the_Family" title="All in the Family">All in the Family</a></i> did years ago."<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Regarding his portrayal as the anti-Semitic Borat, Baron Cohen says the segments are a "dramatic demonstration of how racism feeds on dumb conformity, as much as rabid bigotry", rather than a display of racism by Baron Cohen himself.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> "Borat essentially works as a tool. By himself being anti-Semitic, he lets people lower their guard and expose their own prejudice", Baron Cohen explains.<sup id="cite_ref-rollingstone_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rollingstone-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Addressing the same topic in an <a href="/wiki/NPR" title="NPR">NPR</a> interview with Robert Siegel, Baron Cohen said, "I think that's quite an interesting thing with Borat, which is people really let down their guard with him because they're in a room with somebody who seems to have these outrageous opinions. They sometimes feel much more relaxed about letting their own outrageous, politically incorrect, prejudiced opinions come out."<sup id="cite_ref-npr1_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-npr1-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Baron Cohen, the grandson of a <a href="/wiki/Holocaust_survivor" class="mw-redirect" title="Holocaust survivor">Holocaust survivor</a>, says he also wishes in particular to expose the role of indifference in that <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">genocide</a>. "When I was in university, there was this major historian of the <a href="/wiki/Third_Reich" class="mw-redirect" title="Third Reich">Third Reich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ian_Kershaw" title="Ian Kershaw">Ian Kershaw</a>, who said, 'The path to <a href="/wiki/Auschwitz" class="mw-redirect" title="Auschwitz">Auschwitz</a> was paved with indifference.' I know it's not very funny being a comedian talking about the Holocaust, but it's an interesting idea that not everyone in Germany had to be a raving anti-Semite. They just had to be <a href="/wiki/Apathetic" class="mw-redirect" title="Apathetic">apathetic</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-rollingstone_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rollingstone-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Regarding the enthusiastic response to his song, "<a href="/wiki/In_My_Country_There_Is_Problem" title="In My Country There Is Problem">In My Country There Is Problem</a>" (also known as "Throw the Jew Down the Well"), he says, "Did it reveal that they were anti-Semitic? Perhaps. But maybe it just revealed that they were indifferent to anti-Semitism."<sup id="cite_ref-rollingstone_23-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rollingstone-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Baron Cohen walked onto the runway during the <a href="/wiki/%C3%81gatha_Ruiz_de_la_Prada" title="Ágatha Ruiz de la Prada">Ágatha Ruiz de la Prada</a> fashion show in <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a> on 26 September 2008. In the character of one of his alter-egos Brüno, he was wearing a costume made of <a href="/wiki/Velcro" title="Velcro">velcro</a>. He appeared on the stage with a blanket and items of clothing stuck to his velcro suit. Lights were turned off while security intervened and escorted him off the stage, and the fashion show resumed normally shortly thereafter. Baron Cohen and his team allegedly accessed the fashion show using fake IDs.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lawsuits">Lawsuits</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sacha_Baron_Cohen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Lawsuits">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The government of <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a> threatened Baron Cohen with legal action following the 2005 MTV Europe Music Awards ceremony in <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a>, and the authority in charge of the country's country-code <a href="/wiki/Top-level_domain" title="Top-level domain">top-level domain</a> name removed the website that he had created for his character Borat (previously: http://www.borat.kz) for alleged violation of the law—specifically, registering for the domain under a false name. <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, among others, has reported that Baron Cohen (in character as Borat) replied: "I'd like to state that I have no connection with Mr. Cohen and fully support my government decision to sue this Jew".<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> He was, however, defended by <a href="/wiki/Dariga_Nazarbayeva" title="Dariga Nazarbayeva">Dariga Nazarbayeva</a>, a politician and the daughter of Kazakhstan President <a href="/wiki/Nursultan_Nazarbayev" title="Nursultan Nazarbayev">Nursultan Nazarbayev</a>, who stated, "We should not be afraid of humour and we shouldn't try to control everything..."<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> The deputy foreign minister of Kazakhstan later invited Baron Cohen to visit the country, stating that he could learn that "women drive cars, wine is made of grapes, and Jews are free to go to synagogues".<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> After the success of the <i>Borat</i> film, the Kazakh government, including the president, altered their stance on Baron Cohen's parody, tacitly recognising the invaluable press coverage the controversy created for their country.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Baron Cohen encountered another problem around his Borat character. Two of the three <a href="/wiki/University_of_South_Carolina" title="University of South Carolina">University of South Carolina</a> students who appear in <i>Borat</i> sued the filmmakers, alleging that they were duped into signing release forms while drunk, and that false promises were made that the footage was for a documentary that would never be screened in the US. On 11 December 2006, a <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a> judge denied the pair a restraining order to remove them from the film. The lawsuit was dismissed in February 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 22 May 2009, a charity worker at a seniors' bingo game sued Baron Cohen, claiming an incident shot for <i>Brüno</i> at a charity bingo tournament left her disabled.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> However, the worker later retracted her statement, saying the "actor never struck her", but that he "beat her down emotionally to the point she's now confined to a wheelchair".<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> The scene did not make the final cut for the film. The case was dismissed in late November 2009 on <a href="/wiki/Anti-SLAPP" class="mw-redirect" title="Anti-SLAPP">Anti-SLAPP</a> grounds, with all lawyer's fees to be paid by the charity worker. The dismissal was appealed and upheld on 12 September 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 30 April 2010, <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_Christian" class="mw-redirect" title="Palestinian Christian">Palestinian Christian</a> grocer Ayman Abu Aita, of the <a href="/wiki/West_Bank" title="West Bank">West Bank</a> and former member of <a href="/wiki/Fatah" title="Fatah">Fatah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Br%C3%BCno#Lawsuit_and_death_threats" title="Brüno">filed a lawsuit</a> against Baron Cohen, alleging that he had been <a href="/wiki/Defamed" class="mw-redirect" title="Defamed">defamed</a> by false accusations that he was a terrorist in the movie <i>Bruno</i>. Aita included <a href="/wiki/David_Letterman" title="David Letterman">David Letterman</a> in the suit based on comments made during a 7 July 2009 appearance by Baron Cohen on the <i><a href="/wiki/Late_Show_with_David_Letterman" title="Late Show with David Letterman">Late Show with David Letterman</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> Unlike the other lawsuits, Aita did not sign a release form, and his case centered around whether Baron Cohen's portrayal of Aita was false, not whether he was defrauded.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> In September 2012, the defamation claim was settled out of court for an undisclosed amount, and the court case was dismissed.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2018, former Senate candidate <a href="/wiki/Roy_Moore" title="Roy Moore">Roy Moore</a> (R) of <a href="/wiki/Alabama" title="Alabama">Alabama</a> sued Baron Cohen for $95 million relating to a mock interview in <i>Who is America?</i> and allegations of pedophilia.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_work">Other work</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sacha_Baron_Cohen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Other work">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Baron Cohen <a href="/wiki/Guest-star" class="mw-redirect" title="Guest-star">guest-starred</a> in the fifth season of <i><a href="/wiki/Curb_Your_Enthusiasm" title="Curb Your Enthusiasm">Curb Your Enthusiasm</a></i>, with <a href="/wiki/Dustin_Hoffman" title="Dustin Hoffman">Dustin Hoffman</a>, as a guide to <a href="/wiki/Heaven" title="Heaven">Heaven</a>. He also provided the voice of the <a href="/wiki/Ring-tailed_lemur" title="Ring-tailed lemur">ring-tailed lemur</a> king, <a href="/wiki/King_Julien" class="mw-redirect" title="King Julien">King Julien</a>, in <a href="/wiki/DreamWorks_Animation" title="DreamWorks Animation">DreamWorks Animation</a>'s film series, <i><a href="/wiki/Madagascar_(franchise)" title="Madagascar (franchise)">Madagascar</a></i>, and appeared as <a href="/wiki/Will_Ferrell" title="Will Ferrell">Will Ferrell</a>'s arch rival, the French <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">Formula One</a> speed demon Jean Girard, in the hit <i><a href="/wiki/Talladega_Nights:_The_Ballad_of_Ricky_Bobby" title="Talladega Nights: The Ballad of Ricky Bobby">Talladega Nights: The Ballad of Ricky Bobby</a></i> (2006).<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> He also appeared alongside <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Depp" title="Johnny Depp">Johnny Depp</a> in the film <i><a href="/wiki/Sweeney_Todd:_The_Demon_Barber_of_Fleet_Street_(2007_film)" title="Sweeney Todd: The Demon Barber of Fleet Street (2007 film)">Sweeney Todd: The Demon Barber of Fleet Street</a></i> ,(2007), as Signor Adolfo Pirelli, co-starred in <a href="/wiki/Martin_Scorsese" title="Martin Scorsese">Martin Scorsese</a>'s adventure film <i><a href="/wiki/Hugo_(film)" title="Hugo (film)">Hugo</a></i> (2011), and portrayed <a href="/wiki/Th%C3%A9nardier" class="mw-redirect" title="Thénardier">Thénardier</a> in <a href="/wiki/Les_Mis%C3%A9rables_(2012_film)" title="Les Misérables (2012 film)">the 2012 film version of the musical <i>Les Misérables</i></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Cohen&amp;Others_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cohen&amp;Others-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> He appeared as a <a href="/wiki/BBC_News" title="BBC News">BBC News</a> Anchor in <i><a href="/wiki/Anchorman_2:_The_Legend_Continues" title="Anchorman 2: The Legend Continues">Anchorman 2: The Legend Continues</a></i> (2013).<sup id="cite_ref-Cameos_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cameos-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>For much of the early part of his career Baron Cohen tended to avoid doing interviews out of character. However, in 2004, he did the talk show circuit appearing as himself on <i>Late Show with David Letterman</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Opie_and_Anthony_Show" class="mw-redirect" title="The Opie and Anthony Show">The Opie and Anthony Show</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Howard_Stern_Show" title="The Howard Stern Show">The Howard Stern Show</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> and others in order to promote the forthcoming season of his show on HBO. He was also interviewed on NPR's <i><a href="/wiki/All_Things_Considered" title="All Things Considered">All Things Considered</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-npr1_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-npr1-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> and did an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i>, published in November 2006, that the magazine labelled as "his only interview as himself".<sup id="cite_ref-rollingstone_23-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rollingstone-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> He also appeared in an interview out of character with <a href="/wiki/Terry_Gross" title="Terry Gross">Terry Gross</a> on NPR's <i><a href="/wiki/Fresh_Air" title="Fresh Air">Fresh Air</a></i> on 4 January 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-npr2_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-npr2-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Baron Cohen has twice presented the <a href="/wiki/MTV_Europe_Music_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="MTV Europe Music Awards">MTV Europe Music Awards</a>, first as Ali G on 8 November 2001, in <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>, Germany, and then as Borat on 3 November 2005 in <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a>, Portugal. Baron Cohen appeared out of character to accept an award at the <a href="/wiki/British_Comedy_Awards" title="British Comedy Awards">British Comedy Awards</a> in December 2006. He said at the time that Borat could not make it to the awards as "he's guest of honour at the Holocaust denial conference in Tehran",<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> referring to the <a href="/wiki/International_Conference_to_Review_the_Global_Vision_of_the_Holocaust" title="International Conference to Review the Global Vision of the Holocaust">International Conference to Review the Global Vision of the Holocaust</a>.
</p><p><i>Borat</i> director <a href="/wiki/Larry_Charles" title="Larry Charles">Larry Charles</a> explains that Baron Cohen generally appears in character partly to "protect his weakness", by focusing public interest on his characters rather than himself.<sup id="cite_ref-newsweek_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newsweek-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> His other reason, <i>Newsweek</i> claims, is that Baron Cohen is fiercely private: "...according to the UK press, his publicists denied that he attended a party for the London premiere of <i>Borat</i> and that a party even occurred."<sup id="cite_ref-newsweek_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newsweek-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2010, representatives for Cohen confirmed that he was set to play <a href="/wiki/Freddie_Mercury" title="Freddie Mercury">Freddie Mercury</a> in the <i><a href="/wiki/Bohemian_Rhapsody_(film)" title="Bohemian Rhapsody (film)">Bohemian Rhapsody</a></i> biopic about the rock singer.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> He dropped out of the project in July 2013, citing "creative differences" between him and the surviving members of <a href="/wiki/Queen_(band)" title="Queen (band)">Queen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> Queen guitarist Brian May later said that even though the band and Baron Cohen were on good terms, they felt that Baron Cohen's presence would be "distracting." The role was later played by <a href="/wiki/Rami_Malek" title="Rami Malek">Rami Malek</a>, who earned an <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Actor" title="Academy Award for Best Actor">Academy Award</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Actor_%E2%80%93_Motion_Picture_Drama" title="Golden Globe Award for Best Actor – Motion Picture Drama">Golden Globe Award</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Screen_Actors_Guild_Award_for_Outstanding_Performance_by_a_Male_Actor_in_a_Leading_Role" title="Screen Actors Guild Award for Outstanding Performance by a Male Actor in a Leading Role">Screen Actors Guild Award</a>, and a <a href="/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Actor_in_a_Leading_Role" title="BAFTA Award for Best Actor in a Leading Role">British Academy Film Award</a> for Best Actor.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Baron Cohen shot a spread with <a href="/wiki/Supermodel" title="Supermodel">supermodel</a> <a href="/wiki/Alessandra_Ambrosio" title="Alessandra Ambrosio">Alessandra Ambrosio</a> for <i><a href="/wiki/Marie_Claire" title="Marie Claire">Marie Claire</a></i> magazine to promote the film <i>Brüno</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-elite_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elite-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Sports_Illustrated" title="Sports Illustrated">Sports Illustrated</a></i>'s 6 November 2006 issue contains a column called "Skater vs. Instigator", which illustrates various amusing "parallels" between Baron Cohen and figure skater <a href="/wiki/Sasha_Cohen" title="Sasha Cohen">Sasha Cohen</a>, ranging from their mutually held personal significance of the number 4,<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> to their shared romantic interests in redheads.
</p><p>Baron Cohen was featured in the <a href="/wiki/Time_100" title="Time 100">Time 100</a> list for 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-time_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-time-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2010, Baron Cohen guest-starred in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons" title="The Simpsons">The Simpsons</a></i> episode, "<a href="/wiki/The_Greatest_Story_Ever_D%27ohed" title="The Greatest Story Ever D&#39;ohed">The Greatest Story Ever D'ohed</a>", as Jakob, a quick-tempered Israeli tour guide.
</p><p>In Baron Cohen's <i><a href="/wiki/Grimsby_(film)" title="Grimsby (film)">Grimsby</a></i> (2016; <i>The Brothers Grimsby</i> in the US), he plays the <a href="/wiki/Football_hooligan" class="mw-redirect" title="Football hooligan">football hooligan</a> brother of a British <a href="/wiki/Secret_Intelligence_Service" title="Secret Intelligence Service">MI6</a> spy. The film received mixed reviews from critics and was a <a href="/wiki/Box_office_bomb" class="mw-redirect" title="Box office bomb">failure at the box office</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 3 November 2016, it was announced that Baron Cohen will headline the American <a href="/wiki/Remake" title="Remake">remake</a> of the Danish comedy <i><a href="/wiki/Klown" title="Klown">Klown</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In October 2018, it was announced that Baron Cohen would portray political activist/anarchist <a href="/wiki/Abbie_Hoffman" title="Abbie Hoffman">Abbie Hoffman</a> in the drama film <i>The Trial of the Chicago Seven</i>, with <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Sorkin" title="Aaron Sorkin">Aaron Sorkin</a> set to write and direct.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sacha_Baron_Cohen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Israel_and_Judaism">Israel and Judaism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sacha_Baron_Cohen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Israel and Judaism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Baron Cohen first acted in theatrical productions featuring the <a href="/wiki/Labor_Zionism" title="Labor Zionism">Socialist-Zionist</a> youth movement <a href="/wiki/Habonim_Dror" title="Habonim Dror">Habonim Dror</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He spent a year in <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> <a href="/wiki/Kibbutz_volunteer" title="Kibbutz volunteer">volunteering</a> at <a href="/wiki/Kibbutzim" class="mw-redirect" title="Kibbutzim">Kibbutzim</a> <a href="/wiki/Rosh_HaNikra_(kibbutz)" title="Rosh HaNikra (kibbutz)">Rosh HaNikra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beit_HaEmek" title="Beit HaEmek">Beit HaEmek</a> as part of the Shnat Habonim Dror, as well as taking part in the programme <a href="/wiki/Machon_L%27Madrichei_Chutz_La%27Aretz" title="Machon L&#39;Madrichei Chutz La&#39;Aretz">Machon L'Madrichei Chutz La'Aretz</a> for Jewish youth movement leaders.
</p><p>According to Baron Cohen, "I wouldn't say I am a religious Jew. I am proud of my Jewish identity and there are certain things I do and customs I keep." He tries to keep <a href="/wiki/Kosher" class="mw-redirect" title="Kosher">kosher</a> and attends synagogue about twice a year.<sup id="cite_ref-borateasy_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-borateasy-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marriage_and_family">Marriage and family</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sacha_Baron_Cohen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Marriage and family">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Baron Cohen first met actress <a href="/wiki/Isla_Fisher" title="Isla Fisher">Isla Fisher</a> in 2002, at a party in <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">Sydney</a>, Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> The couple became engaged in 2004. Subsequent to Fisher's <a href="/wiki/Conversion_to_Judaism" title="Conversion to Judaism">conversion to Judaism</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> the two married on 15 March 2010 in <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> in a <a href="/wiki/Chuppah" title="Chuppah">Jewish ceremony</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Baron Cohen and Fisher have three children.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Charitable_donations">Charitable donations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sacha_Baron_Cohen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Charitable donations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 28 December 2015, Baron Cohen and his wife Isla Fisher donated £335,000 ($500,000) to <a href="/wiki/Save_the_Children" title="Save the Children">Save the Children</a> as part of a programme to vaccinate children in northern <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a> against <a href="/wiki/Measles" title="Measles">measles</a>, and the same amount to the <a href="/wiki/International_Rescue_Committee" title="International Rescue Committee">International Rescue Committee</a> also aimed at helping Syrian <a href="/wiki/Refugees" class="mw-redirect" title="Refugees">refugees</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Filmography">Filmography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sacha_Baron_Cohen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Filmography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_videos">Music videos</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sacha_Baron_Cohen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Music videos">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)" title="Madonna (entertainer)">Madonna</a>: "<a href="/wiki/Music_(Madonna_song)" title="Music (Madonna song)">Music</a>" (2000) as Ali G.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bbc_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Accolades">Accolades</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sacha_Baron_Cohen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Accolades">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="box-BLP_sources_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-BLP_sources" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/40px-Ambox_important.svg.png" decoding="async" width="40" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/60px-Ambox_important.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/80px-Ambox_important.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="40" data-file-height="40" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section of a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Biographies_of_living_persons" title="Wikipedia:Biographies of living persons">biography of a living person</a> <b>needs additional <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">citations</a> for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help by adding <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Reliable sources">reliable sources</a>. Contentious material about living persons that is unsourced or poorly sourced <b>must be removed immediately</b>, especially if potentially <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Libel" title="Wikipedia:Libel">libelous</a> or harmful.<br /><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Sacha+Baron+Cohen%22">"Sacha Baron Cohen"</a>&#160;–&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Sacha+Baron+Cohen%22+-wikipedia">news</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Sacha+Baron+Cohen%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers">newspapers</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Sacha+Baron+Cohen%22+-wikipedia">books</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Sacha+Baron+Cohen%22">scholar</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Sacha+Baron+Cohen%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on">JSTOR</a></span></small></span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">September 2016</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<ul><li>1999&#160;– Won <a href="/wiki/British_Comedy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="British Comedy Award">British Comedy Award</a>, Best Male Comedy Newcomer for <i>The 11&#160;O'Clock Show</i> (1998)<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>2000&#160;– Nominated <a href="/wiki/BAFTA" class="mw-redirect" title="BAFTA">BAFTA</a> TV Award, Best Entertainment Performance for <i>The 11&#160;O'Clock Show</i> (1998)<sup id="cite_ref-Saunders_35-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Saunders-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>2000&#160;– Nominated <a href="/wiki/National_Television_Awards" title="National Television Awards">National Television Awards</a>, UK, Most Popular Comedy Performer for <i>Da Ali G Show</i> (2000)</li>
<li>2000&#160;– Won TV Quick Award, TV Personality of the Year for <i>Da Ali G Show</i> (2000)</li>
<li>2001&#160;– Won BAFTA TV Award, Best Comedy (Programme or Series) for <i>Da Ali G Show</i> (2000) (shared)</li>
<li>2001&#160;– Won BAFTA TV Award, Best Comedy Performance for <i>Da Ali G Show</i> (2000)</li>
<li>2003&#160;– Nominated <a href="/wiki/Emmy" class="mw-redirect" title="Emmy">Emmy</a> Award, Outstanding Non-Fiction Program (Alternative) for <i>Da Ali G Show</i> (2003) (shared)</li>
<li>2003&#160;– Nominated Emmy Award, Outstanding Writing for Non-Fiction Programming for <i>Da Ali G Show</i> (2003) (shared)</li>
<li>2004&#160;– Nominated Golden Satellite Award, Best Performance by an Actor in a Series, Comedy or Musical for <i>Da Ali G Show</i> (2003)</li>
<li>2005&#160;– Nominated Emmy Award, Outstanding Variety, Music or Comedy Series for <i>Da Ali G Show</i> (2003) (shared)</li>
<li>2005&#160;– Nominated Emmy Award, Outstanding Writing for a Variety, Music or Comedy Program for <i>Da Ali G Show</i> (2003) (shared)</li>
<li>2006&#160;– Won Ronnie Barker Award<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>2007&#160;– Won MTV Movie Award for Best Kiss alongside Will Ferrell in <i><a href="/wiki/Talladega_Nights:_The_Ballad_of_Ricky_Bobby" title="Talladega Nights: The Ballad of Ricky Bobby">Talladega Nights: The Ballad of Ricky Bobby</a></i></li>
<li>2012&#160;– Won British Comedy Award, Outstanding Achievement Award.<sup id="cite_ref-lifetime_award_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lifetime_award-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Borat_awards_and_nominations"><i>Borat</i> awards and nominations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sacha_Baron_Cohen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Borat awards and nominations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>2006&#160;– Won: <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Film_Critics_Association_Awards_2006" class="mw-redirect" title="Los Angeles Film Critics Association Awards 2006">Los Angeles Film Critics Association Award</a> for Best Actor.</li>
<li>2006&#160;– Won: <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Film_Critics_Circle_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="San Francisco Film Critics Circle Award">San Francisco Film Critics Circle Award</a> for Best Actor.</li>
<li>2006&#160;– Won: <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Film_Critics_Association_Awards_2006" title="Toronto Film Critics Association Awards 2006">Toronto Film Critics Association Award</a> for Best Actor.</li>
<li>2006&#160;– Won: <a href="/wiki/Deutscher_Comedypreis#German_Comedy_Award_2006" title="Deutscher Comedypreis">Deutscher Comedypreis</a> (German comedy award) for Best International Comedy.</li>
<li>2007&#160;– Won: <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden Globe">Golden Globe</a> for Best Actor in a Comedy/Musical</li>
<li>2007&#160;– Nominated: Golden Globe for Best Picture Comedy/Musical.</li>
<li>2007&#160;– Nominated: <a href="/wiki/London_Film_Critics_Circle_Awards_2006" title="London Film Critics Circle Awards 2006">London Film Critics' Circle</a> Award for British Actor of the Year.</li>
<li>2007&#160;– Nominated: <a href="/wiki/Writers_Guild_of_America" title="Writers Guild of America">Writers Guild of America</a> Award for Best Adapted Screenplay (shared).</li>
<li>2007&#160;– Nominated: <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a> for Best Adapted Screenplay (shared).</li>
<li>2007&#160;– Won: <a href="/wiki/MTV_Movie_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="MTV Movie Award">MTV Movie Award</a> for Best Comedic Performance</li>
<li>2007&#160;– Nominated: <a href="/wiki/MTV_Movie_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="MTV Movie Award">MTV Movie Award</a> Nominated for Best Movie</li>
<li>2007&#160;– Nominated: <a href="/wiki/MTV_Movie_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="MTV Movie Award">MTV Movie Award</a> Nominated for Best Fight with <a href="/wiki/Ken_Davitian" title="Ken Davitian">Ken Davitian</a></li>
<li>2007&#160;– Won: <a href="/wiki/Evening_Standard_British_Film_Awards#2006_Winners" title="Evening Standard British Film Awards">Evening Standard British Film Awards</a>: <a href="/wiki/Peter_Sellers" title="Peter Sellers">Peter Sellers</a> award for Best Comedy.</li></ul>
